From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Sun Jul  1 15:53:21 2007
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sun Jul  1 15:53:31 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Laptop Screen hangs after the lid is re-opened
In-Reply-To: <f71236a80706302241s1c379aia5908e698784abb7@mail.gmail.com>
References: <f71236a80706302241s1c379aia5908e698784abb7@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120707010323m64b47619t3b9aaabf55aa084a@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/1/07, Kunal Jain <vertex3d2004@gmail.com> wrote:

>
> I close my laptop's lid expecting either screen to be turned off or
> standby.
> When I re-open the lid, the screen is blank. I have to restart
> ubuntu/fedora. How do I fix this?


"man acpid"

Your laptop has to correctly implement suspend-to-RAM through ACPI for
it work. If it's correctly implemented, closing the lid will cause an ACPI
button event that you can use to initiate suspend-to-RAM, for instance,
by using a userland utility like acpitool. Likewise, you can exit from
the suspend-to-RAM mode either using a lid event, or by pressing the
power-on button.

-Siva

I have a DG 965 RY motherboard, and I have managed to install the following
:
Suse 10.2 +
FC 6+
Ubuntu Feisty +
The above can be installed very normally as they natively support the DG 965
RY.


debian etch might work too.
the common error is about job control/tty being turned off.

I think mehul is probably right.

You will have a problem installing older versions of linux distros on your
computer. I have read that installing silicon drivers may help.

Kamal wrote:
> Hi,   
>     The Linux kernel Version 2.6.21 is more power
> efficient with what is known as 'tickless' kernel.
> Improvements of 15 to 25% have been obtained.
>  For more...
> http://news.com.com/Linux+coders+tackle+power+efficiency/2100-1007_3-6192865.html?tag=txt.caro
> 
> Fedora 7 uses this kernel...
> Interesting developments, especially on the mobile
> front!

Note that this is only on x86 and not x86_64 or other architectures yet. 
There is substantial development that still needs to take place in 
drivers and architecture support before we can see good power management 
improvements. What is currently merged is a good first step.

Rahul

& install from.

suppport structure in India. we Use RedHat AS  v4 in our office  for  a lot

Web Server.  Python scripts power it.

yep...

One way is this,

https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Templates

recently, a team has itself been formed in Launchpad for releasing and
maintaining Ubuntu Theme for drupal..

https://launchpad.net/loco-drupal/

version 5 has been released  :-)

Please note, this theme is for websites who have an official
relationship with Ubuntu or Canonical. If your site has no official
relationship (i.e. you're not a loco or official team website) then you
may use it as a base provided you change the graphic design so that your
website does not confuse people into thinking that you have an official
relationship. See the README.txt for more details.

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Wed Jul  4 13:21:41 2007

Subject: [Ilugc] kubuntu booting problem
In-Reply-To: <465359.18016.qm@web7909.mail.in.yahoo.com>

On Wed, Jul 04, 2007 at 08:38:26AM +0100, Raman.P wrote:
> Please go through installation options in the CD. In debian under
> rescue option, grub can be reinstalled. I am sure ubutunu should have
> such option. You can avoid total reinstall.

In Ubuntu, what you need to do is boot into the live CD, spawn a
shell, mount the drive where the Ubuntu / is present, chroot into it,
and run grub-install /dev/hda (or /dev/sda) and hope for the
best. Works most of the time.

HTH.

Kumar

2007/7/5, Bruce Mathew <brucemathew@gmail.com>:
> Is there any organisation which can support us in imparting FOSS education
> to Schools in Kerala.?

There are many volunteers who already does this. I have been helping
the teachers myself and I have been part of teams who does this during
my college days.
NIT Calicut offers support and training for teachers in the Nadapuram
constituency of Kozhikode district.

See http://fci.wikia.com/wiki/Malappuram/Summer_Camp_April_2007
http://www.pravi.co.nr/2005/01/14/when-teachers-became-students/
http://www.pravi.co.nr/2005/06/08/it-at-school-palakkad-support-group-formation-my-first-talk/


FSF India and SPACE does support IT@School project.

As for commercial support there isn't any yet. But recently signed MoU
between Red Hat and Kerala Government does cover this.

"Red Hat will also train school teachers in Kerala on Linux desktop
skills under a "Train-the-Trainer" program."
http://www.redhat.in/news/article/90.html

Cheers
Praveen

Hello ILUGC,

As some of you already know, Boltzmann Consulting
(India) Pvt. Ltd. http://www.boltzmanninc.com is
hiring a lead web developer to design and build a
feature-rich web application.  Some background on
Boltzmann Consulting and our needs for this project:
Boltzmann is a small but established Chennai company,
we've been doing development work in Chennai for the
past 5+ years but this project will be our first done
entirely using FOSS.  We're interested in talking with
developers who have experience with some or all of the
following:
- Object-oriented design
- Agile, test-driven development
- Ruby on Rails
- XHTML, CSS, AJAX
- Java & GWT
- PPC ads, SEO
- Atom, RSS
- Selenium
- CruiseControl
- Capistrano, Deprec, Monit
- Subversion
- MySQL
- Apache, Lighttpd, Nginx, Mongrel
- and of course Linux

We want to hire a real FOSS technologist with a strong
passion for 'doing it right,' someone who wants to
make their mark building something extraordinary,
expand their expertise and demonstrate their
leadership abilities.  We're flexible about full-time
or part-time work and we care more about ability than
years of experience: this is a great opportunity for
someone looking for their first job as a tech. lead.

If you are interested or know someone who may be,
please contact us:
resumes at boltzmanninc dot com

Thanks,
Suresh Bharathan

hi,
NRC-FOSS is planning to set up a portal to teach tamil - both written  
and spoken. We hope to eventually develop it as a full multimedia  
portal, but will start small with visual first, then add audio. A  
skeleton has been put up at

http://nrcfosshelpline.in/code/wiki/OnlineTamil

if interested, either as a learner or as a teacher, please add your  
ideas and suggestions. Please contact me if you are interested in  
adding/developing content for the portal. Needless to say all  
development will be on the open source model.

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Fri Jul  6 19:13:15 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Fri Jul  6 19:13:25 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] tamil learning course

References: <79A867D8-398F-4C80-A3BD-E04E338B27D0@thenilgiris.com>
	<e3dcb5360707060620v34c4a130mc9f6cc0389c4c560@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d16b1c80707060643g254a887cpe8f912c4daa8caab@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 7/6/07, ?. ???? ??????? <shriramadhas@gmail.com> wrote:
> fine... no more hard writing practise.. then ..  keyboard need to be used..

This can come last in the learning phase.

Initially, learn:

* The alphabets, their pronounciation.
* Commonly used words/phrases/sentences.
* Be able to speak/converse basic sentences with a native speaker.
* Any grammar associate with the above (past/present/present
perfect/future tense).
* Build vocabulary.

One must be able to first learn to speak, comprehend, read, and
finally be able to write/type.

You can also have a look at the Pimsleur approach to learning a language.

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

thanks to all who are responding on this thread. I request you all to  
put your suggestions on the wiki so they dont get lost.

We are planning to start with the alphabets and joining them.

1. Alphabet apears on screen. Click it and the sound comes.
2. Alphabet apears on screen. Click 4 sound symbols and choose the  
correct one
3. Sound is given on click - choose the alphabet
4. (difficult) alphabet is given - user speaks sound into the mic and  
correct/wrong is returned

Next stage, same thing for words, phrases, sentences, paragraphs.

I have never done anything with linux and sound (as i dont like  
music) so am looking for guidance on how to record the sounds and  
edit the sound files.

On Mon, Jul 09, 2007 at 02:43:09AM -0400, Zico wrote:
> Etch stable.

If you don't want to go the compile-from-source way, you have two
options.

1. Not recommended - upgrade to testing/unstable. This will bring in a
   whole set of new packages, but, along with them, many new bugs and
   breakages.
2. Look for it at backports.org. I doubt whether it'll be there now.

Do note that getting a fast moving and huge package set like GNOME in
Debian stable is very tough, given the number of library changes and
dependencies involved in the task. I'd rather settle with the existing
GNOME, unless I really have the time and enthusiasm to go through the
major compile+install procedure. I also would think about the other
Debian GNOME dependencies this might end up breaking.

Kumar
-- 
Kumar Appaiah,

Indian Institute of Technology Madras,
Chennai - 600 036

> Hi.
> i am web running an application in php-linux-apache

> that floder
>  for example
>  let say that i have a Floder name  " Magzine "
>  and if the user type in the folder name as "firstweek"
> and uploads the images. the images will be uploaded to
> 
>  ../Magzine/firtweek/
>                   /img
>                   /thumb
>                  /vedio

> (i.e., the images will be uploaded in the corresponding floders
> /Magzine/firstweek/img , /Magzine/firstweek/thumb and
> /Magzine/firstweek/vedio)
> 
> now the problem is
> 1.the folder "firstweek" is created with the permission as 755 ,even though
> i have set its parent directory's (Magzine) permision to 777

> 2.not able to create the sub folders  (img,thumb,vedio)
> 
> is this  something related to the User ,Group  section in the apache config
> file..?
> 
> 

Making a directory world-writeable is dangerous.
Make the directory Magzine owned by the user that runs Apache and give 
755, that should be enough.

shell> sudo chown `grep '^User' /usr/local/apache/conf/httpd.conf | awk 
'{ print $2 }'` /path/to/Magzine

-- 
Gopal Venkatesan

http://gopalarathnam.com/

On Mon, Jul 09, 2007 at 01:44:56PM +0530, mehul wrote:
> Or use apt-pin and install it from unstable?

Well, I wouldn't really do this for something as big as GNOME, since
many other packages which depend on the GNOME libs will also need to
be pinned (or will be upgraded). In that sense, many packages will
become the testing/unstable ones.

Anyway, if it suits you, you can go ahead and try it, albeit, with
caution, lest you end up breaking the system.

Kumar

Kumar Appaiah,

On Mon, Jul 09, 2007 at 02:40:26PM +0530, Suresh Kumar wrote:
> if($_GET['txtPage']!="")
> {
> $foldername=@mkdir('magzine/'.$weekfol);
> $imagefol=@mkdir('magzine/'.$weekfol.'/img');
> $video=@mkdir('magzine/'.$weekfol.'/video');
> $thumb=@mkdir('magzine/'.$weekfol.'/thumb');
> }

I think the issue is with the permissions of the created directory,
you don't seem to be able to create new directories in the 'magzine'
directory, from what I understand.

As Gopalarathnam has mentioned, make the user who runs Apache the
owner of the directory. Or (unsafe) use chmod to modify the
permissions of the created directory.

Fellow FOSS enthusiasts,

Although i do have a few projects of my own that are open source ,I admit
that i have not had the pleasure of contributing to projects that I do not
own. I think submitting a patch to an existing project is an experience in
itself.And one that I;d love to explore full time. I'd like to
segregate this post into 3 [chunks] of thought.

[1] I'm having a tough time figuring out which open source project to get
involved with that actually encourages new users to submit a patch. No
offence, but in the real world - i only wish i could identify the projects
that could use a helping hand among the ocean of projects - both abroad as
well as in india. Is there a list available , is there an irc channel for
the same ?

[2]To help me answer this question, I figured i would find out from other
users from thus UG - of their first open source project contribution
experience, and how the road to submitting your FIRST PATCH was .

[3] While you're at it , if you know of any open source project that could
use help right away ,do let me know  . I've just quit my job , to take a 10
month opensource stint to broaden my contributions apart from the work i
usually do - ( scripting / javascript ) . I have a project of my own over at
returnable.org , authored the reusable javascript library, and blog on
http://bosky101.blogspot.com . I'd love to work on porting some of the
concepts from event driven programming in javascript and actionscript to
more other/native languages. Possibly even embedded ones.

Any suggestions / experiences shared will be appreciated ,and I hope you
take this mail as a hacker who wants to contribute to existing projects as
much as he wants to create ones on his own 8 )

Keep Clicking,
Bhasker V Kode,
http://advogato.org/person/bkode/
<http://advogato.org/person/bkode/>

On 7/9/07, Bhasker Kode <kode@returnable.org> wrote:
> Fellow FOSS enthusiasts,
>
> Although i do have a few projects of my own that are open source ,I admit
> that i have not had the pleasure of contributing to projects that I do not
> own. I think submitting a patch to an existing project is an experience in
> itself.And one that I;d love to explore full time. I'd like to
> segregate this post into 3 [chunks] of thought.
>
> [1] I'm having a tough time figuring out which open source project to get
> involved with that actually encourages new users to submit a patch. No
> offence, but in the real world - i only wish i could identify the projects
> that could use a helping hand among the ocean of projects - both abroad as
> well as in india. Is there a list available , is there an irc channel for
> the same ?

I do not think anyone will spend time in a dedicated channel meant to
mentor new contributors for all open source projects.

> [2]To help me answer this question, I figured i would find out from other
> users from thus UG - of their first open source project contribution
> experience, and how the road to submitting your FIRST PATCH was .

That depends on project you choose and exposure you already have. If
it is a core development team, it may take time to understand the
process and start contributing patches. But, if it is art work,
documentation or translation team, it is very easy to understand the
process and start contributing patches.

In any case, I highly recommend to subscribe to appropriate mailing
list and be a silent spectator for couple of weeks. You should
understand their process and get used to the way to send patches.

Every organized project may have patch submission guidelines. Please
do not bother to read them before starting to submit patches. First
impression is the best impression. The core developers are more
concerned about the way you send your email. Your email speaks more
than your patch itself.

> [3] While you're at it , if you know of any open source project that could
> use help right away ,do let me know  . I've just quit my job , to take a 10
> month opensource stint to broaden my contributions apart from the work i
> usually do - ( scripting / javascript ) . I have a project of my own over at
> returnable.org , authored the reusable javascript library, and blog on
> http://bosky101.blogspot.com . I'd love to work on porting some of the
> concepts from event driven programming in javascript and actionscript to
> more other/native languages. Possibly even embedded ones.

I'm very sure there is a need for quality contributors in every
project. You will get to know once you understand the processes and
roadmap. The core developers will be friendly and responsive depending
on the confidence you make.

Personally, I've been associated with Ubuntu Documentation team (UDT)
and Subversion. As per UDT is concerned, it is easy to submit patches.
The developers are very friendly. They encourage new comers, even
though they make mistakes. They will explain you howto contribute
patches and things like politely, even though there are so many wiki
pages to answer these type of queries.

As per Subversion is concerned, it is one of highly respected
community. You should observe the dev list for couple of days/weeks.
Once you get to know where you can contribute, you can start
submitting patches. I bet you will find lot of ways to contribute once
you are used to it.

BTW, these are not rules for contributing to open source projects, but
few suggestions based on my experience. These suggestions are not
applicable for thousands of inactive/small open source projects lying
around community sites like sourceforge.net website.

Good luck!
-- 
Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran A
www.livecipher.com
GPG: 0x7A13E5B0

Folks,
          As the title says, linux-2.6.22 has been released today. You
can pick it up from the usual kernel.org mirrors - it hadn't propagated
to the IIT-M mirror as of an hour ago.

    I'm testing the tickless kernel - and I can confirm that there is
no perceptible difference/slowdown in desktop responsivity. You can
leave it configured to tickless by default. The next thing to check is
whether xine/mplayer run as smoothly with a tickless kernel.

-Siva

Message-ID: <3f2beab60707090825r2364425fp4147685b81f1047e@mail.gmail.com>

2007/7/9, Zico <mailzico@gmail.com>:
> Etch stable.

I moved to lenny/testing a while back and now enjoying gnome 2.18 and
whole lot of new apps. I suggest you try testing if it is not a
critical server.

One thing, you will have to keep updating stuff but if you want latest
and greatest it is the best way. Since there is a set of requirements
for packages to move from testing it is sufficiently stable for a
desktop machine.

Just marking it stable won't make it stable right?. Does Ubuntu/Fedora
have the strict checks similar to testing requirements? Some
requirements for a package to move from unstable to testing are

1) no critical bugs during the packages time in unstable (10, 5, 2
depending on priority)
2) All dependencies already in testing
3) buildable on all the supported architectures

It took a while for gnome 2.18 to move to testing because there was
still bugs to be fixed.


Cheers
Praveen

ILUGC Meet (Jul 14th):-
=====================

Time : Sat Jul 14th 15:00 IST 2007
Venue: ADI-TeNeT Seminar Hall,
       #CSD 320, ESB, IIT-Madras.

Map: http://chennailug.org/tenet

Agenda:

> Talk I : Debian Project (40 mins)
Speaker: Kumar Appaiah

This talk will touch upon the beginning of the project, the social
contract, the development cycle (releases, distributions), packaging
and packages, DFSG, the Debian developers, contributing to Debian and
the bug tracking system. 

Link: http://www.debian.org/

> Talk II: Ruby On Rails - An Intro (40 mins)
Speaker: Thyagarajan Shanmugham

This is a talk for freshers and intermediates level audience.  Ruby on
Rails is a web application framework written in the Ruby programming
language, that aims to increase the speed and ease with which Database
-driven web sites can be created and offers skeleton code frameworks
from the outset.

Link: http://www.rubyonrails.org/

HTH :)

From ravi.goglobium at gmail.com  Tue Jul 10 14:32:28 2007
From: ravi.goglobium at gmail.com (Ravi Jaya)
Date: Tue Jul 10 14:32:35 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] thinging serious about mysql then you must know this.
Message-ID: <9d3184460707100202p6b6b1a40tb6e1bb0f6eac6a93@mail.gmail.com>

The derivation of the name MySQL is not clear. Mysql base directory and a
large number of our libraries and tools have had the prefix "my" for well
over 10 years. However, co-founder Monty Widenius's daughter is also named
My. Which of the two gave its name to MySQL is still a mystery, even for us.

The name of the MySQL Dolphin (our logo) is "Sakila,"

Interesting...

we welcome you to share anu funny information like this..

Note: source taken from mysql web site

thanks
Ravi

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Jul 11 16:00:29 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Jul 11 15:49:57 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] File Size change
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0706271126060.2939-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Hi All,

I want to share my recent experience. One application binary file size
was changed suddenly by 500KB. Initially we thought, it may be due to
some virus.

But this size change was happened due to the prelink. During prelink
process, the some lib infos are added into the binary file, just to
reduce the startup time. Get more info from:

man prelink OR http://people.redhat.com/jakub/prelink.pdf

If you know anyother conditions, which will leads to the executable
file size change, Plz share with us.

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

Bharathi we did observe such behaviours. We compared the size of object
files generated at different compilations (code unchanged) and found that
some objects differred in size. We used the 'ls' command to check for the
size.
The same objects if we compared using the 'size' command we found that the
object files we of the same size. All fields we the same.

Ramesh

Install Feisty locally on your machine, use synaptic to download the
packages you need on your machine. Verify that everything is working, then
use APTonCD (http://aptoncd.sourceforge.net/) to burn the downloaded
packages to a CD and give it to your cousin. Will work like a charm.

The other alternative is a huge bunch of volunteer editors willing to
spend time watching for and reverting spam edits.

If you can find out just how many users outside of ilugc you actually
have editing the wiki?  If you take the whole of the ilugc userbase and
generate a login / pass for each of them, you have a good start and can
lock down the wiki, no worries.  Any new member of ilugc automatically
gets wiki posting rights as well.

Makes sense?

Plus a more recent version of Mediawiki might be required... say > 1.5.x . I
guess the version that is used by ilug  Chennai is 1.3.x ?

Another way is making use of built-in anti-spam feature of media wiki:
$wgSpamRegex
It helped in keeping off spam in a wiki i maintain. I got info from this
link:

your mic is mapped to wrong alsa channel. Newer alsa drivers have this
problem. Also, try with line in. Check if line in is working properly.

I can proudly claim that I have been installing fully functional
Ubuntu Linux on all the computers assembled from my company. It used
to take us a lot more effort in getting some aspects working than it
would have if we had tried "other OSes". We have gained a lot of
experience since we started out. Things are so smooth these days that
we install Ubuntu to test the hardware even if the customer insists
that he/she will be installing some "other OS" after purchase. It is a
pity that 95% of the customers go home and install this other OS. We
normally try our best to convince the user that the Linux is going to
be fully functional for all their normal uses (except gaming) and that
piracy is plain illegal.
One problem that we are facing here is the lack of good community
support. We have been finding it very hard to find people good at
Linux. We are planning to contribute our efforts into building a
vibrant Linux community in Trivandrum by offering the services of the
to-be Linux Evangelist (we are still looking for that position) for
the community.

Cheers
Anoop
www.zyxware.com

money for them. So a properly set up and conducted workshop, with  
proper publicity and limit to number of participants will definitely

From rajanvn at gmail.com  Sat Jul 14 09:24:31 2007
From: rajanvn at gmail.com (Natarajan V)
Date: Sat Jul 14 09:24:42 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] cant open /dev/dsp
In-Reply-To: <4CE9BDB7-9E0C-41C6-BC6C-59097256BC99@thenilgiris.com>
References: <4CE9BDB7-9E0C-41C6-BC6C-59097256BC99@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <e977d4310707132054gb7c669bw7c3a53cfe3da24a9@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/13/07, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
> hi
>
> i am going crazy trying to get my microphone to record. Using krec -
> it worked once and only once. When i try to run festival tests i get
> the message: Linux: can't open /dev/dsp. I can hear sound with no
> problem. But not record. No dead/sleeping pids for /dev/dsp either.
> Any clues? System is Mandriva 2007
> --
I am also a KDE fan, and I do do some recordings some times.

If I do not get the mic working, the following are the things that I
check for generally
1. pidof artsd  | xargs kill -- Some times artsd puts a lock on the
sound device. Kill those processes. These will be started again for
each of processes that use the sound system.
2. Open KMix and check the INPUT tab.
        - Make sure the RED Led at the bottom of the MICROPHONE icon
is ON and the MIC has sufficient volume. If you have the Green LED on,
you will hear your own voice on the speaker, which is not suitable for
voice recording.
       - Make sure the CAPTURE has the LED on and also has sufficient volume
       - In the switches tab, make sure you have chosen the right
microphone device and MIC  BOOST LED is ON.

TIP: Personally, I felt Audacity to be better than Krec in terms of
flexibility. In Audacity, you will have to select the driver and the
recording(input device) explicitly.


Regards,
Natarajan

Hi all,

We develop firmware for the next generation networked DVD players which
can connect to your home network (over WiFi and Ethernet), play media
files (video/music/pictures) from your computer/cd/dvd/usb , play radio
over the Internet, etc.. :) Check http://www.z500series.com/ for an example.

We are expanding and are looking for experienced as well as fresh
graduates who have the following skill set.

 - Good communication skills

 - Strong C, C++, Assembler (preferably) skills.

 - Experience with the GNU tool-chain, GNU build-system, general
   GNU/Linux development environment, POSIX API, etc.

 - At the minimum preliminary knowledge of version control systems
   (preferably Subversion)

 - Passionate towards technology (Important)

There is no restraint on salaries for the right candidate. Send your
resumes to sundar@terminus.in

	<B203A156-09DD-4667-A4F7-7260D5373E0D@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <e977d4310707140919j2dbd5beaj2e1bfa258aaeb246@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/14/07, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
>
> On 14-Jul-07, at 9:24 AM, Natarajan V wrote:
>
> > I am also a KDE fan, and I do do some recordings some times.
> >
> > If I do not get the mic working, the following are the things that I
> > check for generally
> > 1. pidof artsd  | xargs kill -- Some times artsd puts a lock on the
> > sound device. Kill those processes. These will be started again for
> > each of processes that use the sound system.
> > 2. Open KMix and check the INPUT tab.
> >        - Make sure the RED Led at the bottom of the MICROPHONE icon
> > is ON and the MIC has sufficient volume. If you have the Green LED on,
> > you will hear your own voice on the speaker, which is not suitable for
> > voice recording.
> >       - Make sure the CAPTURE has the LED on and also has
> > sufficient volume
> >       - In the switches tab, make sure you have chosen the right
> > microphone device and MIC  BOOST LED is ON.
> >
> > TIP: Personally, I felt Audacity to be better than Krec in terms of
> > flexibility. In Audacity, you will have to select the driver and the
> > recording(input device) explicitly.
>
> you are a genius -

Thanks :-)

> followed your instructions and everything worked
> like a charm.

Forgot to mention:
Sometimes the artsd created by Konsole blocks dsp. To overcome this problem try

Konsole -> Settings -> Configure Notifications -> disable all sounds

This will stop giving sounds when you are hitting too many back spaces
in KONSOLE. This has been my major reason behind the locking of dsp at
least on my PC.

Regards,
Natarajan

Just to add, In my box artsd was an evil d(a)emon locking up my audio. I
couldnt run two multimedia applications at the same time. Right now I am
pretty much happy without any artsd support in my box, System sounds
doesnt play but I could always some external program to do that.
You could also get rid of this annoying problem by selecting ALSA as the
default Sound framework from kcontrol. Works like a charm.

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Tue Jul 17 09:54:03 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Tue Jul 17 09:46:41 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] MP3 + Patent issues in Debian
Message-ID: <20070717042402.GC7589@localhost>

Dear ILUGC,

During the last ILUGC meet, it was pointed out that Debian GNU/Linux
has media players which play MP3s out-of-the-box, without additional
codecs. I was wondering why this was so, given that Fedora and Ubuntu
don't allow this.

The reason seems to be because playing (decoding) MP3s by end-users
doesn't seem to warrant any license from the patent owner. See:

http://www.webcitation.org/5MeUrGbFN

This was pointed out to me on debian-user by Carl Fink:

http://lists.debian.org/debian-user/2007/07/msg01486.html

Kumar
-- 
Kumar Appaiah,
462, Jamuna Hostel,
Indian Institute of Technology Madras,
Chennai - 600 036
From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Tue Jul 17 09:57:25 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Tue Jul 17 09:50:03 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] MP3 + Patent issues in Debian
In-Reply-To: <20070717042402.GC7589@localhost>
References: <20070717042402.GC7589@localhost>
Message-ID: <20070717042725.GD7589@localhost>

On Tue, Jul 17, 2007 at 09:54:03AM +0530, Kumar Appaiah wrote:
> The reason seems to be because playing (decoding) MP3s by end-users
> doesn't seem to warrant any license from the patent owner. See:
> 
> http://www.webcitation.org/5MeUrGbFN

Oh, and by the way, if it isn't clear, every other multimedia format
needs codecs, none of which are Debian. www.debian-multimedia.org
exists for this purpose.

Kumar
-- 
Kumar Appaiah,

Indian Institute of Technology Madras,
Chennai - 600 036

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Jul 17 14:57:02 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Jul 17 14:46:48 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: Symposium on Copyleft Revolution
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0707171454130.3954-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

---------- Forwarded message ----------
Date: Tue, 17 Jul 2007 14:37:38 +0530
From: Nagarjuna G. 
Subject: Symposium on copyleft revolution in a conference on  critical geography

Dear friends,

I proposed a symposium on copyleft revolution to this conference to be
held in Mumbai at TISS from 3rd till 7th of Dec 2007.

http://www.5thiccg.org/

Those of you want to speak in the symposium, please submit your
proposals before the end of 20th August 2007.  The shape of the
session will be confirmed by 3rd of September 2007.  The symposium
will accommodate about five speakers on the panel, and the total
duration including at least half-an-hour discussion will be about 2
hours.

Copyleft Revolution

In the last thirty years the role and significance of Information and
Communication Technology have grown significantly, reconfiguring the
spatial logic of modern society. However, it has not remained an
equally accessed base and gone under the control of a few global
corporations that are investing billions of dollars for its
modernisation, impacting the process of knowledge construction and
dissemination for a small section of the society and thereby
transforming other fields of human creativity.  As a response to the
above hegemonistic framework, a parallel cultural and political
movement is under way that is growing at an unprecedented pace and
influencing the way how science, software and other kinds of symbolic
forms are created, published and distributed.  Popularly known as the
Copyleft culture, it is essentially a Free Software Movement that took
off by an innovative use of the existing copyright and by publishing
software under a copyleft license.  This license is meant to give four
fundamental rights to the user of the software published under the
copyleft license: to use it for any purpose, to understand how it
works, to make modifications, and to distribute the modifications.

One of the major outcomes of this revolution is the GNU/Linux
operating system (popularly known by its misnomer, Linux). The
copyleft movement is currently transforming other fields of human
creativity as well---science, poetry, music, cinema and other symbolic
forms. Of these, the most popular success story is Wikipedia.org, the
largest multilingual encyclopedia of the world. There are other, not
yet fully fructified, movements such as public library of science,
open access, creative commons, open music, etc.

The proposed session aims at generating awareness about the Copyleft
movement in general, and discussing its relation to science and
education in particular. While challenging the patent and other
similar systems, it also intends to deliberate on a new model of
development of ICT, centered around collaboration and sharing among
different communities.

Contact address: Nagarjuna G, Homi Bhabha Centre for Science
Education Mumbai, India, nagarjun at gnowledge dot org

HTH
--
Bharathi S

On Tue, 2007-07-17 at 19:16 +0530, Mahalingam Subramaniam wrote:
> Dear All
> My Query is as follows:

> H

get the file size in bytes.. use plain du command


cd /maildir
limit="yourlimitinbytes"
du * | while read size file
do
[ $size -ge $limit ] && echo $file > logfile
done

From sundaram at fedoraproject.org  Wed Jul 18 02:07:48 2007
From: sundaram at fedoraproject.org (Rahul Sundaram)
Date: Wed Jul 18 02:08:02 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] MP3 + Patent issues in Debian
In-Reply-To: <20070717042402.GC7589@localhost>
References: <20070717042402.GC7589@localhost>
Message-ID: <469D289C.1040702@fedoraproject.org>

Kumar Appaiah wrote:
> Dear ILUGC,
> 
> During the last ILUGC meet, it was pointed out that Debian GNU/Linux
> has media players which play MP3s out-of-the-box, without additional
> codecs. I was wondering why this was so, given that Fedora and Ubuntu
> don't allow this.
> 
> The reason seems to be because playing (decoding) MP3s by end-users
> doesn't seem to warrant any license from the patent owner. See:
> 
> http://www.webcitation.org/5MeUrGbFN

IANAL but note that a FAQ is not considered a legal document and the FAQ 
does not really answer whether a Free software decoder requires a patent 
license or not.  You need a written explicit agreement from the patent 
holder according to GPLv2 section 7.  The real answer is probably that 
Debian is not a commercial entity and is unlikely to sued and even if 
sued the consequences are a court injunction to stop distribution and 
not monetary liability.

> This was pointed out to me on debian-user by Carl Fink:
> 
> http://lists.debian.org/debian-user/2007/07/msg01486.html

Debian itself might be a non commercial activity but use in commercial 
contexts would void that argument.

Rahul

Yeah, few of us assisted them at times. But he may have got certain
things done which he expected from us. Perhaps, it was due to luggers
availability of time and other commitments. Infact, I talked to him
about the support offered by Ilugc members, but I think he's less
convinced.

Overall, his idea was to showcase employee's contribution and
recognize their efforts. Remember most of them are windows users, new
to linux. Now imagine the kind of difficulty and resistance they had
while migrating to linux. Their opinion about this success is very
important than any one else.

I hope he have mentioned about Novell's contribution to this effort.
I'm yet to view the final draft posted at Youtube, as the site is
prohibited to visit from IIT - Mumbai.  But, I'll take a look at it as
early as possible.

FWIW, ELCOT is the topmost client for Novell with more than 40,000
SuSE desktops. They surpassed Fujifilm which is using 8000 SuSE
desktops. Now, Novell have appointed a residential engineer at ELCOT
for providing corporate support. Infact, Novell is also planning to
recruit more enthusiastic free software developers (even freshers) to
provide support for ELCOT from their premise.

Given the input (mailstorage.txt):

shell> cat mailstorage.txt
140K /abcde/fghij/w001/wesley
26M /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/wilson
1G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/alok
2G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/john

The following is the output I get with GNU awk on RHEL 4.4:

shell> awk '$1 ~ /[1-9][0-9]*G/ { print $0 }' mailstorage.txt
1G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/alok
2G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/john

The following is the output I get with nawk on FreeBSD 4.11:

shell> nawk '$1 ~ /[1-9][0-9]*G/ { print $0 }' mailstorage.txt
1G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/alok
2G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/john

Is your input in the above format?  If yes, what awk is your system 
running and what is the output?

Hi,

On 7/18/07, Zico <mailzico@gmail.com> wrote:
> You respect copyright and against *piracy*????

Yes.

Get to the basics?

Any work/code that you do is your copyright. License determines how
you distribute copies of your work/code.

Stealing a document that prohibits its re-distribution is against
copyright law, and is copyright infringement.

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright_infringement

> Then what type of question do
> you people accept? One guy asked you about *tighten* his pdf and you
> answered that, "We are in open source...."

You can use PGP/GPG to encrypt documents and send it. It is security.
Nothing wrong with it.

> and now i asked you about
> *breaking password of pdf*

This is illegal. Because, you are stealing someone else's copyrighted
work that doesn't allow free distribution.

Welcome to the real world!

> and you answered * We respect copyright and are
> against *piracy* .... blah blah...." Then what should some one ask
> you????????

You might want to be more polite in future, and cut down your tone a
bit especially when you are going through a learning curve.

Regards,

From: Gopal Venkatesan <gopal@gopalarathnam.com>
To: ILUG-C <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>
Date: Wed, 18 Jul 2007 11:19:59 +0530
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] shell script
Mahalingam Subramaniam wrote:
> Dear Gopal 
> awk '$1 ~ /[1-9][0-9]*G/ { print $0 }' mailstorage.txt
> the above suggested shell command is not generating the desired output on the output file. kindly do the needful.
> with thanks
> 
Given the input (mailstorage.txt):
shell> cat mailstorage.txt
140K /abcde/fghij/w001/wesley
26M /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/wilson
1G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/alok
2G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/john
The following is the output I get with GNU awk on RHEL 4.4:
shell> awk '$1 ~ /[1-9][0-9]*G/ { print $0 }' mailstorage.txt
1G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/alok
2G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/john
The following is the output I get with nawk on FreeBSD 4.11:
shell> nawk '$1 ~ /[1-9][0-9]*G/ { print $0 }' mailstorage.txt
1G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/alok
2G /mnopq/rstuvwx/w001/john
Is your input in the above format? If yes, what awk is your system 
running and what is the output?

From pravi.a at gmail.com  Wed Jul 18 14:33:04 2007
From: pravi.a at gmail.com (Praveen A)
Date: Wed Jul 18 14:33:12 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Boot two distros from the same DVD..
In-Reply-To: <3f2beab60706180024j8235e8dt3cb54f1ba40af81b@mail.gmail.com>
References: <be4915c60706172355r3267fc03se75210f873ea4674@mail.gmail.com>
	<3f2beab60706180024j8235e8dt3cb54f1ba40af81b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3f2beab60707180203g4839a349h7d4886883c6e59fb@mail.gmail.com>

2007/6/18, Praveen A <pravi.a@gmail.com>:
> 2007/6/18, Sivabalan Thirunavukkarasu <siva886@gmail.com>:
> > I have separate ISO images of Fedora 7 (size : 2.7 GB) and
> > UbuntuStudio (867 MB).. is it possible to write both the isos or files
> > on the same DVD and to choose anyone of the OS while booting from the
> > DVD..
>
> Yes. I remember seeing it in last foss.in DVD.  I think Shanu (cced
> here) created that DVD.
>
> Shanu,
>
>  Can you tell Shiva how you made it?

Shanu has shared the tip. Thanks for sharing this.

Dont remember much offhand - but it was something as below:

- Copy out the bootable floppy images for each OS to the iso
- Create a isolinux which reference the bootable floppy images
- Pass kernel load arguements to use ramdisk as the root FS
- Copy out all the installation packages to the iso preserving the
 layout.
- build images using mkisofs
- Use qemu to test the iso image
- Burn when happy

Cheers
Praveen

From anoopjohn at gmail.com  Wed Jul 18 22:41:50 2007
From: anoopjohn at gmail.com (Anoop John)
Date: Wed Jul 18 22:42:01 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] graphic problem
In-Reply-To: <1b91e5ae0707180815q6d4d502ahc4089484b64baa41@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1b91e5ae0707180815q6d4d502ahc4089484b64baa41@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <406f1f3f0707181011u7cd89280p9af484b46025476f@mail.gmail.com>

> I had recently installed Ubuntu 7.04 (Feisty Fawn) in pentium 4 with
> intel 82845G Graphic onboard adpator,512MB RAM, and 80GB Hard disk,
> after installation it takes about 15 minutes to boot and the screen
> remains blank while booting (black screen).

I think all Intel chipsets are supported in ubuntu. I installed ubuntu
7.04 on an Intel 946G board today. The card was detected and installed
during startup. However when in re-ran dpkg-reconfigure on
xserver-xorg it failed to detect the card and reverted to a VESA
driver. I then had to manually edit the xorg.conf to change back to
the intel driver. Perhaps you should check your xorg.conf file to see
if the right driver has been loaded. If the driver has not been
installed you can install it with
sudo apt-get install xserver-xorg-video-intel
Cheers
Anoop
www.zyxware.com

From: stylesen at gmail.com (Senthil Kumaran S)
Date: Thu Jul 19 11:13:50 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Reg vpnclient
In-Reply-To: <8C997BC0B110FE5-11DC-5281@MBLK-M06.sysops.aol.com>
References: <8C997BC0B110FE5-11DC-5281@MBLK-M06.sysops.aol.com>
Message-ID: <5ef2113c0707182243v58935aa0w4d9f865dbda249fa@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/19/07, arunvelusamy@aim.com <arunvelusamy@aim.com> wrote:
> arun@arun-laptop:~$ sudo /etc/init.d/vpnclient_init status

Oops. It seems like the proprietary VPN client provided by Cisco
systems. Why dont you try "vpnc" it works like a charm in
Ubuntu/Debian/RedHat/*. All you need to do is this:

Configuring VPN Client in GNU/Linux

Step 1: Install vpnc in your GNU/Linux box. You need not restart the
machine after installing vpnc :)

For FC* users:

# sudo yum install vpnc

For Ubuntu/Debian users:

# sudo apt-get install vpnc

Step 2: Create a configuration file /etc/vpnc/myvpnc.conf with
the following content.

IPSec gateway 214.x.x.x
IPSec ID MyCompany
IPSec secret xxxxxxxx
Xauth username yourusername
Xauth password yourpassword

The last two lines is optional if you want to give the
username/password each time you want to login to the VPN then remove
the last two lines.

Step 3: Start the VPN client using the following command.

# vpnc /etc/vpnc/myvpnc.conf

Step 4: To disconnect the client

# vpnc-disconnect

If you have any trouble in installing vpnc, you can try obtaining the
source package from http://www.unix-ag.uni-kl.de/~massar/vpnc/ and try
compiling the source.

HTH :)

-- 
Senthil Kumaran S
http://www.stylesen.org

   DHCP server listens on port 67 for lease requests. But why the DHCP

traffic is broadcast. Or is there any other reason for that.

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Thu Jul 19 15:28:42 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Jul 19 15:28:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] why DHCP client port should be fixed
In-Reply-To: <d5deb2390707190244x563225acve32325586b0dd875@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d5deb2390707190244x563225acve32325586b0dd875@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d16b1c80707190258q17be9f7atdee068cc44247d5d@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 7/19/07, VenkataRavikanth <venkataravikanth@gmail.com> wrote:
>    DHCP server listens on port 67 for lease requests. But why the DHCP
> client also should use the designated port 68 to interact with the server.

1. Because it follows RFC 2131:
http://www.faqs.org/rfcs/rfc2131.html

2. It is mandatory to follow standards.

So, if you move to a different network and if they use DHCP, you know
it will be running on the same port, rather than you having to go ask
someone about it.

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

I understand why the server uses standard port 67. But whats the need
for the server to send the response to the port 68 of client ? In a
typical client server communication, client can initiate the request
from any of its port and server responds back on the same port. Please
see the below link

I am of the opinion that RFC never says anything to be mandatory.

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Thu Jul 19 20:27:52 2007

Hi,

On 7/19/07, VenkataRavikanth <venkataravikanth@gmail.com> wrote:
> I understand why the server uses standard port 67. But whats the need
> for the server to send the response to the port 68 of client ?

Because you may have a firewall on the server that allows UDP only for
certain ports?

> In a
> typical client server communication, client can initiate the request
> from any of its port and server responds back on the same port.

True.

> Please
> see the below link

Good! You are doing your homework.

> http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DHCP#DHCP_and_firewalls

There is your answer.

> I am of the opinion that RFC never says anything to be mandatory.

RFCs start off as proposals, and then IETF approves them as standards:
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Request_for_comments

But, it is important to follow Free/Open standards, because it is a
standard, and everyone can follow it.

SK

> I think all Intel chipsets are supported in ubuntu. I installed ubuntu
> 7.04 on an Intel 946G board today. The card was detected and installed
> during startup. However when in re-ran dpkg-reconfigure on
> xserver-xorg it failed to detect the card and reverted to a VESA
> driver. I then had to manually edit the xorg.conf to change back to
> the intel driver. Perhaps you should check your xorg.conf file to see
> if the right driver has been loaded. If the driver has not been
> installed you can install it with
> sudo apt-get install xserver-xorg-video-intel
> Cheers

On 7/19/2007 10:15 PM, ??????? wrote:

> hope what konqueror is offering is sort of a web-based system administration.. 
> or is it browser based system administration..

What konqueror offers you is a browser based view of a set of GUI system
admin tools. Kind of like control panel on windows.

> came across few softies like webmin, directadmin etc., that are used for web 
> based system admin purposes..

Web based interfaces that frontend perl scripts that make config changes
in servers (quite often by adding / removing values from text files or
populating sql databases)

	srs

Hi,

On 7/20/07, santhosh kumar <sanleoit@gmail.com> wrote:
> How to reinstall Grub?

Google around for solutions?

> first i have installed linux, afterwards i install WindowsXP ;
> Now my system is not with linux,

The GNU/Linux partition still exists. Just that windoze bootloader got
installed to the MBR without even asking your permission.

> Please give some suggestion to reload Grub without reinstalling XP;

Why do you need to reinstall xp to reload grub? Just restore grub to
MBR. For a start:
http://www.sorgonet.com/linux/grubrestore/

http://www.whoopis.com/howtos/howto_restore_mbr_grub.php

Message-ID: <b658fbda0707200447v7b1e0920k368a1e7d3143a14a@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,
     Windows should be installed FIRST then Linux (Fedora, SuSE,
RedHAT..etc).
     As per my knowledge / experience
     Bcoz. windows boot loader does not support linux booting.
     But linux bootloader(GRUB, LILO) - its supporting windows booting
through GRUB, LILO. while installing linux it will add automatically winwos
into bootloader. if require u can edit grub.conf  as per your windows
partition.

note: if you want load linux, u can use linux bootable CD.

Siva

From gshah at efrontier.com  Fri Jul 20 17:37:23 2007
From: gshah at efrontier.com (Gourav Shah)
Date: Fri Jul 20 17:38:44 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] How to load Grub?
In-Reply-To: <9328ba920707200430j7900b8e6x281f35df3233bef7@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9328ba920707200430j7900b8e6x281f35df3233bef7@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <46A0A57B.2080400@efrontier.com>


> Please give some suggestion to reload Grub without reinstalling XP;
>
This is the guide if you are using ubuntu. But should work for other
distros as well with a little figuring out....
https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RecoveringUbuntuAfterInstallingWindows?action=show&redirect=RecoverGrub


Basic steps are ,
1.  Boot from the live cd/recovery cd
2. check which partition is your linux root , mount root
3.  mount /boot if you have a separate partition.
4. finally reinstall grub   , here is the example of the command that i
would use if my linux root is mounted on /mnt/root and  my hard disk
device is  /dev/hda
grub-install --root-directory=/mnt/root /dev/hda


for more details, check out the help page.

~gshah

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Fri Jul 20 20:43:20 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Fri Jul 20 20:43:30 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] W3c-html-validator on debian
In-Reply-To: <203338.89170.qm@web8910.mail.in.yahoo.com>
References: <203338.89170.qm@web8910.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <a0c4f6270707200813t265380dke0160d8cea401e8f@mail.gmail.com>

On 20/07/07, Satheesh Kumar wrote:
> hi,
> Sorry for asking this silly question.

It isn't silly!

> I have installed w3c-html-validator in Debian[etch] i don know how to launch the application or how to start with. Any one help to proceed. I don' even know how to get the man page related to that.

Here's how I figure it out:
apt-cache show w3c-markup-validator says somethings, of which this is
significant:
"This is a CGI script which ..."

So, you need to spawn the script as a CGI script.

A cursory glance at the package's file list reveals something:
http://packages.debian.org/cgi-bin/search_contents.pl?searchmode=filelist&word=w3c-markup-validator&version=stable&arch=all

Notice the following:
/usr/lib/cgi-bin/check

So, you must have a web server (apache2) running, and all you do is visit
http://localhost/cgi-bin/check

and you should get the check page. Also, if you had URLs (URIs)
pointing to the W3C Validator's web address, you can change them to
the above localhost/cgi-bin/check, and they should work.

HTH.

Kumar (Debian fan ;-)

From mehul.forums at gmail.com  Sat Jul 21 15:05:33 2007
From: mehul.forums at gmail.com (mehul)
Date: Sat Jul 21 15:05:43 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] ubuntu-mouse problem
In-Reply-To: <1c81e6720707210207j7c9c3629gd12e25e6b79cf91d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1c81e6720707210207j7c9c3629gd12e25e6b79cf91d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <1375fd8a0707210235s2a018947uaebe426a92bb9d80@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/21/07, Bruce Mathew <brucemathew@gmail.com> wrote:
> Dear Friends
>
> I installed Ubuntu and SUSE but my mouse is not working. The mouse if serial
> One and i have only 256 MB memory. Is it a problm.

Go to tty1 by pressing ctrl + alt + F1, login there and type
sudo /dev/input/mouse or /dev/mouse.
It could also be mice or mouse0 or some such instead of
mouse. There could be more than one, you may need to try
many of them.
Does it show some junk characters? If it does then mouse
is detected by the OS but problem is with X configuration.
Do you have windows? Does the mouse work under
windows?
What make of mouse it is?

Subject: [Ilugc] Problem in connecting Tata Indicom LG 350T phone
In-Reply-To: <200707201145.06360.kushaldas@gmail.com>

Message-ID: <feff2f50707220049t5e5fb323ub33a16e92fc6405b@mail.gmail.com>

Here is my Wvdial.conf to connect using my Tata indicom phone. Hope this
helps

Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
Baud = 115200
Init1= AT+CRM=1
Phone = #777
Username = Internet
Password = Internet
Stupid Mode = 1
Compuserve = 0
Idle Seconds =300

On 7/20/07, Kushal Das <kushaldas@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Hi,
> I am trying to connect Tata Indicom LG 350T phone , using wvdial.
> This is my wvdial.conf file:
> [Modem0]
> Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
> Baud = 115200
> SetVolume = 0
> Dial Command = ATDT
> Init1 = ATZ
> SlowControl = Hardware (CRTSCTS)
> [Dialer Defaults]
> Username = Internet
> Password = Internet
> Phone = #777
> Stupid Mode = 1
> Inherits = Modem0
>
> Then when I am trying to dial
>

> --> Cannot get information for serial port.
> --> Initializing modem.

> ATZ
> OK

From prabhu at aero.iitb.ac.in  Sun Jul 22 17:49:21 2007
From: prabhu at aero.iitb.ac.in (Prabhu Ramachandran)
Date: Sun Jul 22 18:20:47 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [JOB] Building Open Source weather visualization tools 
Message-ID: <18083.19273.905621.749834@gargle.gargle.HOWL>

Hello,

[Apologies for the cross-posting!]

Project positions are open at the Department of Aerospace Engineering,
IIT Bombay for the visualization of weather data using open source
tools. The project will involve creating tools for the visualization
of atmospheric weather data using MayaVi. MayaVi is an open source,
interactive, 3D visualization tool written in Python. More information
on MayaVi is available from http://mayavi.sourceforge.net.

In addition to directly working with MayaVi and its core development
team, the project will require working with and contributing to
several important open source projects like VTK (http://www.vtk.org),
Python (http://www.python.org), Traits and the Envisage application
framework (http://code.enthought.com).

We are looking for people with the following skills:

 * knowledge of C and object oriented programming with C++.
 * passion for 3D graphics, visualization, software engineering and
   technology.
 * passion for open source software.
 * knowledge of Python is a plus.

Qualifications:  Basic BE/B.Tech./BSc/BCA degree

Duration of project:           2007 to 2009.

More details are available here:

 http://www.aero.iitb.ac.in/~prabhu/Projects


Regards,
--
Prabhu Ramachandran                 http://www.aero.iitb.ac.in/~prabhu
From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Sun Jul 22 22:58:27 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Jul 22 22:58:35 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] USB Simply Buffered, and GNU/Linux
Message-ID: <d16b1c80707221028w3cd6c06fub9d62cf1f8f2ca53@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

I have written USB Simply Buffered (USB) to introduce gnubies to USB
and libusb using GNU/Linux:

* Device Enumeration:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/usb/usb-de-0.3.pdf

* Mass Storage Class - Bulk Only Transport:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/usb/usb-msc-0.2.pdf

The documentation was prepared using OpenOffice 2.0. The corresponding
.odt files are available here (if anyone would like to improve it):

http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/usb/usb-de-0.3.odt

http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/usb/usb-msc-0.2.odt

* USB device enumeration teaching code examples, using libusb [1]:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/usb/de-code-0.1.tar.gz

Appreciate any feedback,

Regards,

SK

[1] libusb. http://libusb.sourceforge.net/.

From kushaldas at gmail.com  Sun Jul 22 22:56:19 2007
From: kushaldas at gmail.com (Kushal Das)
Date: Sun Jul 22 23:02:04 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Chotha Beta 1 released (A wordpress client)
Message-ID: <200707222256.19779.kushaldas@gmail.com>

Hi,
Chotha Beta 1 is released. Chotha is a blog client written in PyQt4. This is 
mainly for wordpress, will add support for others later. It is having basic 
HTML tag editing capabilities with saving blog entries locally in the system. 
You can also save it as draft in the server. You can preview your entry 
either in Firefox or in Konqueror. Or else you can click and go to visual 
mode to see quick preview (without images).

Screenshot: http://flickr.com/photos/kushaldas/870308314/

Webpage: http://sourceforge.net/projects/chotha


To understand the meaning of the name please ask any of your Bengali friend :p
Comments are welcome :)

Note: Few major bugs like layout one is there knowingly.

Kushal Das
-- 
Fedora Ambassador, India
http://kushaldas.in

Hi All,

Here is some feed back we collected about the event last week.
 
cheers
Senthil
 
Good Job!!!
--------------
 
1) The free software event was really useful. In fact, I got to know the
origin of free software and the correct meaning "free" software only
after attending the event.
 
The pot-luck was always really good, particularly the chicken dish. :-) 
 
Most importantly, I met many people at the session and exchange of ideas
was great.
    --Sayeed
 
2)Congratulations! on organising such a great event..
I think the presentation was fabulous. It was very well made and was put
across in a a way where it made an impact.
 
Meeting up to exchange ideas and finding out what people are upto is a
good idea.
 
Was great to be a part of the event..
 
 ---Ashwini
 
1) Thanks to all others who organised the event. For me it was a great
exposure. Even getting soemthing as basic as -free as in freedom and not
free as in freebies is what FS means was very exciting. 
 
2) Yes, we have switched one computer at office to Ubuntu already,
thanks to the session and Ashish's high energy levels. Hopefully Balaji
will be able to make it to office on Saturday and we can figure out an
equivalent for SPSS and how to work smoothly on open office spreadsheet
also and then our transition would be complete. 
 
The film and presentation were quite good!
 

Thanks 
Best 
kamayani 
 
Need to improve
-----------------
3) 
I felt people were still apprehensive about various applications running
on Linux. Lot of time went in trying to convince that such (e.g.: Baraha
kind of
documentation) things (i.e, not the Baraha tool as such) are indeed
available. 
It would have been easy if you just showed how to it. When there is a
specific query, better demonstrate right away, if possible. For example,
it was so simple to demonstrate the USB stick works.
In summary, come prepared to run few applications and interface device
access.  These are the fundamental things that people expect in a demo
like this.
 
The presentation was useful to me.
 
 -Ravi A
>> point taken ! will show kannada stuff nex time

Message-ID: <3c52da3c0707222352p667035a1x59e533c2366f6400@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/23/07, Bruce Mathew <brucemathew@gmail.com> wrote:
> Dear Friends
>
>
> My OS is windows XP with 256 MB memory - But i put my Ubuntu Live CD and the
> machine stuck without any Mouse Movements.
>
> My mouse is logitech Make and a serial One..[ with wider PIns ]
>

And which version of Ubuntu? I used to have a similar problem with a
logitech serial mouse on an older computer with older distros (<Etch,
Dapper, I don't know whether the newer ones detect it). It used to
wrongly detect my mouse as PS/2.

One option is to install using the Alternate Install CD, and then
manually modify /etc/X11/xorg.conf to use the correct mouse device (I
think /dev/ttyS0 or /dev/ttyS1 depending on which serial port) and
protocol. It may be possible to do this using a Live CD too - perhaps
going to Ctrl+Alt+F1 and modifying /etc/X11/xorg.conf and restarting
X...

HTH

--Arnold

Yeah. Bits and bytes, and a lot of them too.

> One point - may be good to include some of this documentation as HTML as

I wanted something that:

- I could use as a presentation for technical talks.
- Can be read offline, and doesn't depend on Internet connectivity/bandwidth.

> Something in a Wiki
> style or like in the PHP help pages would be even better... so that people

- doesn't depend on PHP-database connectivity, else, I have to manage
it or ask someone to do that for me (and I don't have time for that).

> can contribute sample source code snippets and the like against specific
> sections.

I have released it under GNU Free Documentation License, and anyone is
welcome to use the template.

In fact, one can even do similar presentations for say, networking
packets. A good documentation project for final year students.

Date: Mon Jul 23 15:24:08 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] ubuntu-mouse problem
In-Reply-To: <1c81e6720707222045y4eb5944dhd34aab8bd6b9effe@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <400483.24422.qm@web51009.mail.re2.yahoo.com>


--- Bruce Mathew <brucemathew@gmail.com> wrote:

> Dear Friends
> 
> 
> My OS is windows XP with 256 MB memory - But i put
> my Ubuntu Live CD and the
> machine stuck without any Mouse Movements.
> 
> My mouse is logitech Make and a serial One..[ with
> wider PIns ]
> 
> -- 
If you are using a serial mouse on a computer with
ps/2 mouse socket .most live CDs will not detect the
serial mouse , as the ps/2 socket will be detected and
mouse will get mounted there.Some live CDs might not
even start.
Solution is to get a ps/2 mouse or serial to ps/2
adapter,the former is easier to get.
TPD.

On Mon, Jul 23, 2007 at 10:17:00PM +0800, Satheesh Kumar wrote:
> Yeah Thanks Appaiah,

You're welcome, but Kumar will be preferable.

>        Failed validation, 78 errors
> 
> but on using the firefox add-on as specified by one of the luggies
> i am getting  12 errors.
> moreover  the errors doesn't seem to overlap too..
> 
> which  one should i rely upon??

I would *always* rely on the W3C HTML validator, sicne it's the simple
reason that it's the very test you have to pass to be compliant. Also,
some errors are shown twice by the validator, in that if you fix one
problem, your number of errors usually reduces by two or three.

All the best!

Kumar

From sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in  Tue Jul 24 11:30:01 2007
From: sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in (sriram)
Date: Tue Jul 24 11:30:23 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: : FOSS Tools for Dissertation Writing
References: <cdc8c4430707222344j13914e1ax8a5e6eddc6761063@mail.gmail.com>
	<d16b1c80707222354n59c75821y5fbd7842cd91a524@mail.gmail.com>
	<cdc8c4430707222358j1604cc6dq763f555a03cb77f1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <loom.20070724T074806-46@post.gmane.org>

Ramanathan Muthaiah <rus.cahimb@...> writes:
> Thanks Shakthi. Google search, "Dissertation writing + FLOSS tools"
> came up with 128,000 results with the first being this :
> 
> http://www.educationaltechnology.ca/couros/308

ok, you got answers, but the other answers on the list are not quite complete. 
procite (not prosite) is really a bibliography management tool, something that 
is used in addition to the basic writing tool for your dissertation. 
openoffice would be a writing tool but it does not have great bibliography 
management tools. latex would be a good choice for you to do the basic writing 
and bibtex will then do the bibliography (like procite). unless you have a 
large number of citations which are culled from an even larger bibliography 
source or are using search engines to find your bibliography material, it may 
be easier to avoid bibtex altogether - simply extract all the biblio material 
and cut and paste them into latex files.

sriram

mehul wrote:
> On 7/24/07, Rahul Sundaram <sundaram@fedoraproject.org> wrote:
>> Neither the DVD or Live images would have the complete set of packages
>> in the repository but see http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/Fedora7/FAQ for
>> details.
> 
> This is quite bad in my opinion, what about users who don't have both
> good bandwidth and DVD drive? There are many such people around.

To be more explicit, Fedora never included all the packages in the 
repository even in previous releases. What you had was "Fedora Core" in 
the media while "Fedora Extras" was only available in the repository. 
The merge of these two repositories amounts to around 8000 packages in 
around 9 GB. That would nearly a dozen CD's with a number of obscure 
packages. Still, the above FAQ does link to atleast one retail vendor 
who offers such a pack.

> Is something like apt-on-cd around for Fedora? Then this move does
> make a bit more sense.

http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/FWN/Issue97#head-af7f7608a0fe7e84d627646e03930750a0495c46

Rahul

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Jul 24 18:49:32 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Jul 24 18:49:44 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re:  can't install tomcat in debian
Message-ID: <55444.61.247.255.57.1185283172.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

Sometimes the problems on Linux with Java is because of how most
distributions have gcj installed.. and /usr/bin/java and /usr/bin/javac
are using that.

When you install Sun JDK on your linux machine, a good idea would be to
rename the /usr/bin/java symlink to something like /usr/bin/java_gcj and
you could rename /usr/bin/javac to /usr/bin/javac_gcj.

You could then set the path of the Sun JDK into your default system path.
Also, please do set the JAVA_HOME setting to point to the directory where
your JRE or the JDK are installed.

That should fix the problem with your tomcat install.

By the way, someone had asked the question about Swing not working on
Linux. This will solve that problem too.

PK

On 7/24/07, ?. ???? ??????? <amachu@ubuntu.com> wrote:
> http://www.alfresco.com/

Alfresco is an Enterprise Content Management system. There is subtle
difference between normal CMS like drupal and Alfresco. The primary
use of Alfresco is to manage documents, work flow, etc in an
organization. Recently they have introduced Web Content Management.
But if the OP is looking for a lightweight CMS to just manage a
website, then Alfresco is not the right choice.

From amartyo at gmail.com  Wed Jul 25 17:45:44 2007
From: amartyo at gmail.com (amartyo banerjee)
Date: Wed Jul 25 17:45:56 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Server at work most probably compromised,
	need suggestions for what to do next
Message-ID: <3b15edbe0707250515m40b97842ib63c740f3c63ae13@mail.gmail.com>

Hello everyone,

A box at work which acts as a subversion server has most probably been
compromised /rooted.

I'll try to mention below how and why I have come to that conclusion.
It's a bit long so please bear with me. I hope to get suggestions from
ilugc about how to gather more evidence if necessary, and what to do
going forward.

The box in question runs Fedora Core 6 and has subversion and apache2
installed on it. Developers access the subversion repository through
http. Everything is behind a firewall of course. I'm not sure of all
the details because I'm not an administrator.

What I do know is that there is one external consultant who also has
access rights to the subversion repository and often works from remote
locations. To enable him to access the repository from outside,
changes were made to the firewall to grant access to the standard http
ports on the subversion box. Access to other ports was not granted, as
far as I knew.

Yesterday evening a problem was first noticed when someone had to
login as root on the server and could not because the password had
changed. Nobody knew who had done this. The password was reset by
rebooting, going into the grub menu, making the server boot in single
user mode, then resetting.

After that a look at /root/.bash_history showed that somebody while
logged in as root had changed the root password, and then created two
ordinary users with the same uid and gid as root, i.e 0, plus one user
with an ordinary uid and gid.

This looked to me like a clear sign that the box had been rooted.

Looking through /var/log/secure* showed that from about midnight on
Jul 18 there were many attempts to bruteforce usernames and passwords
to get ssh access. This was surprising because although sshd was
running on the box, I thought the firewall was not forwarding any
requests to it.

>From the timestamps of the failed ssh login attempts it looks like
some kind of script was running each time, because there were many
failed attempts from the same IP address just 3 - 4 seconds apart.

Finally between 7:43 and 7:45 hrs on July 19th there were two
successful ssh logins as root.  This too was surprising because I
thought root login was not permitted by default in ssh. However 'man
sshd_config' says that the default value of 'PermitRootLogin' is
'yes'.

About 15 minutes after the successful root login there is a successful
login with the same username as one of those 'special' usernames with
uid and gid 0 mentioned earlier.

Looking in the home dir of these new users showed executables with
strange names that don't seem legitimate.

On trying to find out why it was that ssh on this server was visible
to the outside world, this is what seems to have transpired:
Initially, the subversion server was not accessible from outside the
firewall. At some point, when it had to be made accessible, an
external IP address was assigned to the server, along with it's
internal private IP address. The server has only one NIC, and the
administrators could not make it have 2 addresses at once.

Instead what they did was setup a rule on the firewall, such that if
requests for the assigned external IP on the http ports came to the
firewall, they were just forwarded to the internal IP address of the
server.

At some point due to physical relocation of the server from one office
to another, the assigned external IP had to be changed. When this was
done the consultant could no longer access the subversion repository.
The problem was somewhat strange in that if one used a browser to try
to connect to the repository, one was prompted for the subversion
password and could then browse the repository, but connecting with the
commandline 'svn' client would fail with a message about 'PROPFIND'
request failed.

Finally, as a last resort all 65K+ ports were opened up, i.e.. any
requests on the new external IP on any port were allowed through. This
solved the subversion access problem, but at a cost. Now ssh requests
on this address were passed through too.

Looking at /var/log/secure* shows that the time for the first failed
connection attempt to ssh corresponds roughly with the time all ports
were opened up.

ssh being accessible from the outside world, combined with the default
setting permitting root login, combined with a trivially easy password
resulted in the box being compromised, or so it seems to me.

I have saved copies of everything under /var/log, root's .bash_history
plus everything in the homedirs of the users created by the intruder.
I also did an rpm -V on all installed rpms. I didn't notice any
altered system binaries, but lots of config file changes. These could
well be legitimate changes made internally, I see no way to tell. I
also searched for all files owned by these new users, but that
returned what seem to be false positives because these users have the
same uid and gid as root.

I also searched for setgid and setuid files in the /home directory. I
didn't find any setuid files, but in backups of the subversion
repository, I find that in each copy the dirs db, db/transactions,
db/revs and db/revprops are all setgid. I don't know if this is
legitimate or not.

Thank you if you have read this far. My detective work, such as it is,
is based on the following articles in linuxjournal that I read a long
time back:
http://www.linuxjournal.com/article/5348
http://www.linuxjournal.com/article/5347
http://www.linuxjournal.com/article/5346
http://www.linuxjournal.com/article/5345
http://www.linuxjournal.com/article/5344
http://www.linuxjournal.com/article/5343

I am not a sysadmin, yet I found myself in the strange position of
doing all this figuring out and telling others including the admins
here what I've found.

Anyway, now for my questions:
What else is there that could be done to investigate how much damage
has been done?
What else should be saved as evidence?
I assume the box will have to be rebuilt, so how can one be sure which
if any of the  backups of the subversion repository are trustworthy ?
I think that perhaps using dd to take an image of the whole disk might
be useful for forensic purposes, is there another better way to do
that?
Should one report this incident to CERT-In or CERT or is it not worth
the trouble?

I haven't pasted any of the log files I based my conclusions on in
this mail. Should I paste them on pastebin.com or something like that
for the list to see?
 Should I just grep and paste what I think is relevant out of the log
files etc or paste them whole?
What about legit usernames and other data that probably should not be
made public?

Thanks for reading this far. I really need help with this problem.

amartyo

On 7/25/2007 5:45 PM, amartyo banerjee wrote:

> A box at work which acts as a subversion server has most probably been
> compromised /rooted.

Yes. And congratulations for doing the forensics you have done so far.

The most likely cause does seem to be an ssh dictionary attack based on
what you describe here.

> Finally between 7:43 and 7:45 hrs on July 19th there were two
> successful ssh logins as root.  This too was surprising because I
> thought root login was not permitted by default in ssh. However 'man
> sshd_config' says that the default value of 'PermitRootLogin' is
> 'yes'.

You can blame RMS for this :)  Typical unix implementations allow su to
root only from users in the 'wheel' group. This was not implemented in
the GNU version as RMS didnt like the idea. That philosophy seems to
have carried on to ssh logins as root as well.

Try ssh to root on a freebsd box and it just won't let you do that.

> What else is there that could be done to investigate how much damage
> has been done?

Well, the guy rootkitted you, installed some random malware that is
either sending out spam, or carrying out ddos attacks, or hosting an
ircbot to coordinate such stuff .. or maybe a dns and web server for a
spammer's porn and pill sites

> I assume the box will have to be rebuilt, so how can one be sure which
> if any of the  backups of the subversion repository are trustworthy ?

Dont trust anything on the box. Especially after the date when all the
ports were opened up.  I am reasonably sure you made backups of that svn
repository?  Rebuild the box from scratch. Restore from backup.

And make sure that firewall policies are not tampered with just because
one developer wants to access svn remotely from home. Set up an ssh
gateway on a separate IP, that he can ssh to (with a key) and setup an
ssh tunnel to the subversion box from there.

http://svn.haxx.se/users/archive-2004-03/1145.shtml

Tortoisessh has a svn tunnel mode too, if I'm not wrong.

> Should one report this incident to CERT-In or CERT or is it not worth
> the trouble?

It is a group of DoT babus. Sure, they are supposed to investigate it,
and I would be interested to see what they do with the stuff you hand
them .. so go ahead and send them an image if you like.

	srs
From joe_steeve at gmx.net  Wed Jul 25 18:38:23 2007
From: joe_steeve at gmx.net (Joe Steeve)

	message of "Wed\, 25 Jul 2007 18\:21\:45 +0530")
References: <3b15edbe0707250515m40b97842ib63c740f3c63ae13@mail.gmail.com>
	<46A74761.60405@frodo.hserus.net>
Message-ID: <86ejiwpr5k.fsf@lark.home>

Suresh Ramasubramanian <linux@frodo.hserus.net> writes:
> And make sure that firewall policies are not tampered with just
> because one developer wants to access svn remotely from
> home. Set up an ssh gateway on a separate IP, that he can ssh to
> (with a key) and setup an ssh tunnel to the subversion box from
> there.

Also., making sshd listen on a non-standard port avoids scripted
shh attacks to an extent. Most of the dumb scripts will only check
the standard-ssh-port. Seeing that your standard-ssh-port is not
open they'll move on to the next machine they can find.

Also using iptables to block incoming connections on the machine
itself makes it less reliant on another firewall box's
configuration.

Monday-Sunday, and the rows having the days. All tasks are entered in

- Red: High priority
- Blue: Medium priority
- Black: Low priority

From mohan.tux at gmail.com  Wed Jul 25 20:36:11 2007

amartyo banerjee wrote:
> Hello everyone,
> 
> A box at work which acts as a subversion server has most probably been
> compromised /rooted.
As many have said, I'd:
1. rebuild the m/c.
2. separate svn from ssh gateway.
3. make ssh login key based and disable password based login. What I'd 
done was to have key based OpenVPN tunnels and route between subnets for 
external access. Thus only UDP ports for OpenVPN were forwarded. This 
enabled us run ssh on std ports for the LAN and not open it up to the 
external world.
4. If http access was for svn access, that also could have been secured 
using htpasswd. Every hurdle you add decreases chances of /root 
exponentially. Helps to be paranoid.

Preferable if you set up another machine and move this offline for 
further analysis. Impressed with what you collected not being the 
sysadmin. Normal sysadmin activity in our co included checking messages, 
syslog and wtmp/last everyday to check overnight activity. Apart from 
other things, sysadmin must check critical files everyday. Glancing 
thro' itself will throw up unusual activity.

Mohan

>
>
> Funny thing though - it's likely that the intrusion would never have been
> detected if the intruder had not changed the root password. I for one
> do not run fam or tripwire or any such stuff, and would not have noticed
> anything suspicious until I started running out of disk space or
> something.
>

Believe me, there are other ways of noticing intrusions. At one time,
I used to have a VA-Linux PC running RH6.2 and was regularly
connecting to the net using an earthlink dialup account. A cracker got
into the system using a weakly secured account (the ftp user, iirc) -
I noticed some rather strange, but friendly messages on xconsole, and
it took me a while to realize that it was not ET. :-D

Cheers
Ramaswamy

At last intel is in open-source world.

*
"Intel Software Dispatch have announced the availability of the Threading
Building Blocks (TBB) template library under the
GPL<http://threadingbuildingblocks.org/>v2 with the run-time exception
-- so this previously commercial only package
is now open for all the use, whether for open-source projects or commercial
offerings (although they are explicitly encouraging open source use). The
interface is more task-based then thread-based, but with a somewhat
different view of things than, e.g. OpenMP <http://www.openmp.org/>. From
the Intel release: 'Intel(r) Threading Building Blocks (TBB) offers a rich and
complete approach to expressing parallelism in a C++ program. It is a
library that helps you leverage multi-core processor performance without
having to be a threading expert. Threading Building Blocks is not just a
threads-replacement library. It represents a higher-level, task-based
parallelism that abstracts platform details and threading mechanism for
performance and

From bhuvan at ubuntu.com  Thu Jul 26 10:22:10 2007
From: bhuvan at ubuntu.com (Bhuvaneswaran A)
Date: Thu Jul 26 10:22:22 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Reading a Tar file
In-Reply-To: <200680.89734.qm@web54105.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
References: <200680.89734.qm@web54105.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4dc6c9040707252152i3a538be3t398c613b21292544@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/26/07, Ashok Antony <anjeas_net@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Hi All,
>
>
>     I had a data file which is very huge in size. so I just tar that file.
>
> now I would like to read that content of the file without untar'ing that.
>
> Is there anyway in which can I do that ?

If you mean reading file names in the archive, you can use this command:

$ tar tvf file.tar.gz

or, if you mean reading content of specific files, you can store
filenames (one file name with full path per line) to extract in a
seperate file, extract-list.txt and run following command:

$ tar zxvf file.tar.gz -T extract-list.txt

-- 
Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran A
www.livecipher.com
GPG: 0x7A13E5B0
