Subject: [Ilugc] Reading a Tar file
In-Reply-To: <200680.89734.qm@web54105.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
References: <200680.89734.qm@web54105.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3c52da3c0707260225w50d3043dhe144df3290187d00@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/26/07, Ashok Antony <anjeas_net@yahoo.com> wrote:
>     I had a data file which is very huge in size. so I just tar that file.

tar does not do any compression.

> now I would like to read that content of the file without untar'ing that.
>
> Is there anyway in which can I do that ?
>

If you are looking for compression you can perhaps use gzip, and then
use zcat to do what you intend to.
$ gzip largefile
$ zcat largefile.gz

--arnie
From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Jul 26 19:19:25 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Jul 26 19:07:45 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: Release of LX installer for Debian GNU/Hurd
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0707261915030.10386-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

A student team in MES Engineering College, Kuttippuram, Kerala,
successfully finished the New Installer for Debian GNU/Hurd. This
Installer is named as LX, since it is a sucesser of Debian Hurd K
series installer & it directly boot into X.

The Team members of the Installer Project are available at
http://www.projecthurd.tk

About Debian GNU/Hurd: The Hurd is a set of servers running on top of
the GNU Mach microkernel to implement file systems, network protocols,
file access control, and other features that are implemented by the
Unix kernel or similar kernels (such as Linux). Together they build
the base for the GNU OS. Debian GNU/Hurd is a distro of GNU OS Under
Development for developer, server and desktop platforms.

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S

Subject: [Ilugc] Server at work most probably compromised,
	need suggestions for what to do next
In-Reply-To: <46A766E3.6040909@gmail.com>
References: <3b15edbe0707250515m40b97842ib63c740f3c63ae13@mail.gmail.com>
	<46A766E3.6040909@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3b15edbe0707260712x6217d5cdx86c0dfdb08fb7e1e@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 7/25/07, Mohan Sundaram <mohan.tux@gmail.com> wrote:
> amartyo banerjee wrote:
> > Hello everyone,
> >
> > A box at work which acts as a subversion server has most probably been
> > compromised /rooted.
> As many have said, I'd:
> 1. rebuild the m/c.
> 2. separate svn from ssh gateway.
> 3. make ssh login key based and disable password based login. What I'd
> done was to have key based OpenVPN tunnels and route between subnets for
> external access. Thus only UDP ports for OpenVPN were forwarded. This
> enabled us run ssh on std ports for the LAN and not open it up to the
> external world.
> 4. If http access was for svn access, that also could have been secured
> using htpasswd. Every hurdle you add decreases chances of /root
> exponentially. Helps to be paranoid.
>

Many many thanks to everyone to who has replied so far with their
suggestions for what to do and for sharing their own experiences.

I've forwarded all these emails to my boss, who'll be ensuring that
something along the lines of the suggestions given so far is carried
out.

Please do mention anything else that comes to mind, and anybody else
with something to add who hasn't done it so far, please chime in. The
more inputs there are, the better the chances of the right thing being
done at work.

> Preferable if you set up another machine and move this offline for
> further analysis.

I was thinking along similar lines.
Set up another box, set the repository up using the last good backup,
and for the compromised box, take if offline, hook up another disk of
same or bigger size and take an image with dd. Make sure the network
config is done right this time for the new box. Something like that?
Also, see if CERT-In does anything with the disk image.

>Impressed with what you collected not being the
> sysadmin.

Thanks for the kind words.

>Normal sysadmin activity in our co included checking messages,
> syslog and wtmp/last everyday to check overnight activity. Apart from
> other things, sysadmin must check critical files everyday. Glancing
> thro' itself will throw up unusual activity.
>

Well, that's a whole different can of worms. :( You've put your finger
on a sore spot allright. I'm not sure it should be discussed here.
Maybe offline and in person, assuming I meet people who've posted to
this thread at the next ILUGC meet or something. Or atleast not on the
list, but via private mail. If anybody is interested I'll open to
doing either.
From ambuj.mbp at gmail.com  Thu Jul 26 20:10:43 2007
From: ambuj.mbp at gmail.com (Ambuj Thacker)
Date: Thu Jul 26 20:10:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] opensuse after installation
Message-ID: <c021e3c90707260740t58d5cb3ckc4f4c4a85771c03f@mail.gmail.com>

Today I upgraded 3 systems from opensuse 10.1 to 10.1.Menu launcher in KDE
is good,but the default main menu launcher in GNOME was not that user
friendly.For people who want to change it:-
Go to panel and right click on it.Click on "Add to panel"-> "Traditional
Main menu" to get the old drop down menu instead of the defaut "computer"
that appears default in SUSE.

One more problem in ALL the 3 computers was in the menu.lst file which is
present in /boot/grub. Windows entry was "chainloader (hd0,1)+1" change it
to "chainloader +1" to boot into windows.

aMBUJ
    :)

On 27/07/07, Praveen A wrote:
> Switch to Linux!
>
> GNU/Linux, or simply Linux, is an alternative to Microsoft Windows. It

I disagree. This isn't the USP of GNU/Linux. GNU/Linux is a complete
system, userland+kernel with a _wide_ variety of applications (from a
distribution perspective).

> is easy to use and gives more freedom to users. Anyone can install it:

I am "mixed" on this. It is tough to install GNU/Linux, at least the
first time, with frightening keywords like logical partition,
/dev/hda5, boot loader on Master boot record etc. Sounds much tougher
than "C drive", "D drive" etc.

> Linux is free as in freedom, and often available free of charge.

I agree. No doubt about this! :-)

Anyway, the website maintainer has presented his or her views, and I
don't fully agree with it. But as such the content of the website is
lucid and clear, and is worth recommending.

Kumar

In Ubuntu 7.04 the icon of the folder can be changed easily..Here is how..

Right click on the folder->Properties->Basic->Click on the default folder
icon.Browse to the new icon and click open.The best part is that you can
also select the .jpg image for the icon :O

What about just using some lightweight distro like DSL, Puppy?
They hardly take up any hard disk space or RAM, they can be
easily used for lightweight work.
Or just use it as some kind of a server, which won't require too
much processing power. If slackware's website can run on a P3
800MHz, I don't think too much will be required for say an
internal website if such a need is there.
If you just need to experiment, you can use setup a small LAN
between the 3 of them and try out some networking concepts
just to learn them.

Hi Luggies,

This is one of my experience I had with GNU/Linux. I have a quad boot
Sempron system running FC3, Ubuntu, Windows XP and Windows ME (all OSs
installed on a single 120 GB IDE HDD). The system was working fine for
the past 3 years when XP has started giving trouble. The said XP is
installed on a 20GB NTFS partition. The trouble began 2 months back
when there was a power surge while running XP crashing the NTFS
partition.  After that the NTFS partiton became unreadable (according
to Windows). The XP installer is not even recognizing that partition
and am unable to even repair that dead OS (or go for a clean install).

All my files were locked in NTFS partition. The rescue came from FC3
which is setup to read the NTFS partition. FC3 was able to read that
partition like a charm recovering all the files. Luckily I was able to
backup the files. But, I don't understand when XP installer has
trouble in examining my disk, how can the FC3's NTFS driver able to
make it.

Even I tried installing Windows 2000, even that died. It is already 2
months without XP, while the other OS's  (FC3, Ubuntu and Windows ME)
works without any problem. I suspect some change in my partition
table. But not sure of it. When I started the system from the scratch
it had 8 partitions (7 FAT32(1 for Windows ME which was active), 1
NTFS (XP Partition)). When I installed FC3 I made 1 /boot (primary
partition) and / partition (ext 3 logical). When I installed Ubuntu I
added 2 more ext3 partitions (1 for ubuntu / and other for general
purpose, both logical partition). Before the installation of FC3  the
Win ME FAT32 partition was made as active boot partition. After FC3
installation /boot has became the 1st partition on the disk making  it
as a active boot partition. So, I have a doubt here that XP installer
is trying to search for a active Windows partition as the first
partition or else it dies. But, I am not sure about this.  This
clearly indicates that the XP installer is a real crap. My disk is
nearly 98% full may be this also confuses XP installer I think. But
why can't it give a clear information instead of saying "Examining
Disk................" for a longer time.

Hi,

On 7/28/07, Ambuj Thacker <ambuj.mbp@gmail.com> wrote:
> we should not get away with your old PC`s carelessly rather we should try to
> find out a possible solution to reuse them till we can.

1. Try the LinuxBIOS project:
http://linuxbios.org/Welcome_to_LinuxBIOS

2. Try SimpleOS. I have fixed SimpleOS bugs for gcc 4.1.2.
http://www.shakthimaan.com/downloads/sos/simpleos-25jul2007.tar.gz

You can try the examples from grub. The twelve articles on OS concepts
were written in French by David Decotigny and Thomas Petazzoni, and
published in (GNU/) Linux Magazine between 2002-2004:
http://sos.enix.org/fr/PagePrincipale

If anyone knows French, and can translate the articles to English, it
will be valuable with the source code.

Shakthi Kannan

google - probably googlefs.  but with companies that have been in operation
that long, like us, and yahoo, you're more likely going to see nfs being
used 

And while in our case we do use linux fileservers on a large scale, a
lot of what we use is netapp filers (storage area network - SAN) and
maxtor filers (network attached storage / NAS) .. and nfs plays an
important role in clustering these together.

Subject: [Ilugc] M$ reinvents bittorent.....8D
Message-ID: <69621d830707291113l2bbbe126naef1b7a4cf4ac256@mail.gmail.com>

Anon E. Muss writes "Microsoft has a new Secure Content Downloader tool that
sounds an awful lot like a Bittorrent clone. It's described as a
'peer-assisted technology' where '[e]ach client downloads content by
exchanging parts of the file they're interested in with other clients, in
addition to downloading parts from the server.' Right now MSCD is just a
time-limited preview, intended to support downloads of select Microsoft beta
releases (e.g. Visual Studio 2008). If this test goes well, Microsoft will
probably start using MSCD for all their large downloads. How do you feel
about subsidizing Microsoft's bandwidth costs?"

Read more of this
story<http://developers.slashdot.org/article.pl?sid=07/07/28/1631205&from=rss>at
Slashdot.

8-D

it depends on are you allowed to split the files and do the process.
Some type of data mining require normalization done on the whole file.
In such cases you will have to effectively make a parse tree by storing data
on disk rather than memory.

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Tue Jul 31 09:07:15 2007
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Tue Jul 31 09:19:11 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Parsing Large Log Files which is of size ~1GB
In-Reply-To: <dc538c3f0707300953s728725bfp344035fb8a332610@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dc538c3f0707300421x52593fb9j16629acee3c70dc7@mail.gmail.com>
	<b2600ec40707300905j71758b9cm8a5db699be314cdd@mail.gmail.com>
	<dc538c3f0707300953s728725bfp344035fb8a332610@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070731033715.GA14209@frodo.hserus.net.hserus.net>

On Mon, Jul 30, 2007 at 10:23:48PM +0530, balachandar muruganantham wrote:
>the logs are generated on the production box where large no of
>requests come. i should not  bring the system down but i should also
>know the log details so that i can monitor the server.

If your production traffic logs that much, you should look at logging it to
a separate / dedicated log server (nothing fancy,  as long as there's
plenty of disk). That can also run log analysis processes.

Just having daemons write that much log onto a server that's also handling
production traffic is a serious performance hit. And then trying to parse
those logs when the server is up and serving stuff is another serious
performance hit.

From arnstein87 at gmail.com  Tue Jul 31 18:36:37 2007
From: arnstein87 at gmail.com (Arnold Noronha)
Date: Tue Jul 31 18:36:47 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Not able to ping two ethernet interfaces connected
	through cross cable in same PC.
In-Reply-To: <8d2abdcb0707310341s38c8482dhdd03a27000450e6@mail.gmail.com>
References: <8d2abdcb0707310341s38c8482dhdd03a27000450e6@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3c52da3c0707310606q56438676p65981bd039f6a727@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/31/07, Bhavesh Kamani <kamanibhavesh@gmail.com> wrote:
>     #route add -net 192.168.0.5 netmask 255.255.255.0 gw 192.168.0.5 dev
> eth0
>     #route add -net 192.168.0.1 netmask 255.255.255.0 gw 192.168.0.1 dev
> eth1

You're trying to create two routes for 192.168.0.x?   I'm not a
networking expert, but this seems wrong. try:

# route add -net 192.168.0.5 netmask 255.255.255.255 gw 192.168.0.5 dev eth0
# route add -net 192.168.0.1 netmask 255.255.255.255 gw 192.168.0.1 dev eth1

HTH,
--Arnie

For Documents & Settings just copy you home directory from old machine to
new machine.
For software, if you used apt-get or synaptic then use APTonCD (
http://aptoncd.sourceforge.net/) to burn all the downloaded package and
install it on the new machine.
